The Implication of an Impossible Antecedent
Author argues that an impossible composite does not imply its part.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why an impossible antecedent can imply a contradictory consequent and how this affects the necessary implication between a composite and its part.

Core Idea
An impossible antecedent does not necessarily imply its parts; it can imply their negation.

This passage delves into a nuanced logical problem: if a composite (majmu') is impossible, does it still imply its parts? The author argues that it does not, because an impossible antecedent can imply the separation of the part, not the part itself. This challenges the assumption that the composite necessarily implies its component parts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim under scrutiny
The claim is that the composite implies one of its parts (al-majmu' yalzim minhu tahqquq ahadihima). This is a common logical principle.
2
Consider the impossibility case
The author introduces the possibility that the composite itself is impossible (muhal). Under that supposition, the antecedent (the composite) is impossible.
Impossible here means logically contradictory or empirically unrealizable.
3
Trace the implication of the impossible
Based on the principle that an impossible thing can imply another impossible thing (jawaz istilzam al-muhal muhalan), if the composite is impossible, it can imply the separation of the part (nifak al-juz'), which is also impossible.
This shows that implication does not require a possible antecedent.
4
Draw the conclusion
The composite does not necessarily imply the part (fala yastilzim al-juz'). The author affirms this as the correct view (wa huwa al-haqq).
This refutes the naive claim of necessary implication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المجموع تحقق أحدهما ؛ لجواز استحالة المجموع الذي هو المقدم، فعلى تقدير ثبوته ينفك عن الجزء؛ بناء على جواز استلزام المحال محالا، فلا يستلزم الجزء، وهو الحق. ولا يبعد أن يقال: إن استلزام الكل للجزء ضروري، وإنكاره مكابرة، غاية ما في الباب استحالة المقدم توجب استلزامه لانفكاك الجزء أيضا، ولا استحالة فيه؛ فإن غاية ما لزم منه صدق شرطيتين، تالي أحدهما مناف لتالي الأخرى. هذا، وهو موضع تأمل، والعلم الحقيقي عند واهب العلوم. بقي شيء، وهو أنا ندعي ذلك اللزوم الجزئي بين كل أمرين واقعيين، ونبرهن عليه بأخذ تلك الكلية باعتبار التقادير الواقعية. فنقول: كلما تحقق مجموع أمرين واقعيين على كل واحد واحد من التقادير الواقعية تحقق أحدهما على تلك التقادير، وكلما تحقق مجموع أمرين واقعيين على تلك التقادير تحقق الآخر، فبعض ما تحقق أحد الأمرين الواقعيين تحقق الآخر على بعض التقادير الواقعية، فبطل الاتفاقية الكلية الخاصة التي حكم فيها بموافقة صدق التالي صدق المقدم على جميع التقادير الواقعية من غير لزوم أصلا، كما هو المشهور، أو من غير معلومية اللزوم من غير وساطة العلم بالاتفاق، فتأمل؛ فإنه دقيق.
The composite [implies] the realization of one of its parts; because of the possibility of the impossibility of the composite which is the antecedent. So upon the supposition of its existence, it becomes separated from the part, based on the permissibility of the impossible implying the impossible, so it does not imply the part. That is the truth. And it is not far-fetched to say: The implication of the whole for the part is necessary, and its denial is obstinacy; the most that can be said is that the impossibility of the antecedent necessitates its implying the separation of the part as well, and there is no impossibility in that; for at most it entails the truth of two conditionals, the consequent of one contradicting the consequent of the other. This is a place for reflection, and true knowledge is with the Bestower of sciences. There remains something: We claim that partial implication between every two actual things, and we prove it by taking that universality with consideration of actual suppositions. We say: Whenever a sum of two actual things is realized under every single actual supposition, one of them is realized under those suppositions, and whenever a sum of two actual things is realized under those suppositions, the other is realized. So some of what is realized of one of the two actual things, the other is realized under some of the actual suppositions. Thus the special universal accidental agreement is invalidated, in which it is judged that the truth of the consequent agrees with the truth of the antecedent under all actual suppositions without any implication at all, as is well known, or without known implication without the mediation of knowledge of agreement. So reflect; for it is subtle.
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary on a prior claim about implication (luzum) between a composite and its part. The author addresses a specific objection: if the composite (majmu') is impossible, can it still imply its part? The argument proceeds in stages. First, the author states that the composite's realization implies one of its parts, but if the composite is impossible, then on the supposition of its existence (impossible), it would be divorced from the part, because an impossible thing can imply another impossible thing. Thus the composite does not necessarily imply the part. This is the correct view. Then the author considers an opposing claim: that the implication of the whole for the part is necessary, and denying it is obstinate. The counter is that even if the antecedent is impossible, it implies the separation of the part, which is not impossible; it only results in two conditional statements with contradictory consequents. The author leaves this as a matter for reflection. Next, the author proposes a specific claim: they assert a partial implication between any two actual (real) things, and they prove it by considering universality under actual suppositions. The proof: If a sum of two actual things is realized under all actual suppositions, then each part is realized under those suppositions. But this leads to the invalidation of 'special universal accidental agreement' (al-ittifaqiyya al-kulliyya al-khassa), where the truth of the consequent always matches the truth of the antecedent without any implication (luzum) at all, or without known implication. This is the target of the critique. The author concludes with an exhortation to reflect, noting the subtlety.

المجموع
اللزوم
المحال

B) The separation of the part.

Key Takeaway
An impossible antecedent can imply a contradictory consequent, undermining the claim that a composite necessarily implies its parts.

Invalidating Universal Accidental Agreement
Author invalidates the special universal accidental agreement with a logical proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the proof against the special universal accidental agreement and evaluate its validity.

Core Idea
Universal accidental agreement is invalid because it fails under the actual suppositions of impossible antecedents.

The author now turns to a direct refutation of the 'special universal accidental agreement' (al-ittifaqiyya al-kulliyya al-khassa). This is the view that for any two actual things, the truth of one always accompanies the truth of the other under all actual suppositions, without any necessary implication. The author constructs a logical proof to show that this agreement cannot hold.

Guided Path
1
Understand the target doctrine
The special universal accidental agreement states that whenever the antecedent (matter/composite) is true under all actual suppositions, the consequent is also true under those suppositions, but without any necessary connection (luzum).
It is a form of correlation, not causation.
2
Examine the proof against it
The author begins: 'We claim that there is partial implication between every two actual things.' This is a stronger claim of implication (luzum juz'i). To prove it, he takes universality with consideration of actual suppositions.
The proof uses the method of suppositional reasoning (taqdir).
3
Follow the logical steps
The proof: If a sum of two actual things is realized under every single actual supposition, then each part is realized under those suppositions. But then it would also be true that under some suppositions, one part is realized and the other is not, contradicting the universal agreement.
This shows that the universal agreement cannot be universal without contradiction.
4
Conclude the invalidation
Therefore, the special universal accidental agreement is invalid (fabtala al-ittifaqiyya al-kulliyya al-khassa). The author emphasizes that this is a subtle point and urges reflection.
The agreement fails because it assumes implication without necessity, but the proof shows necessity (or partial implication) exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Definition of Contradiction in Mantiq
Author defines contradiction as two things one of which negates the other.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the defining condition for two things to be contradictories (naqīḍān) according to the Mantiq tradition.

Core Idea
Two things are contradictories when one is the negation of the other.

This lesson unpacks the precise definition of contradiction. The author states that any two things—whether concepts or assents—are contradictories if one is the negation of the other. This is the foundational rule for identifying contradictory pairs in logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
The author defines the term 'contradictories' (naqīḍān). Locate the phrase that introduces what is being defined.
The definiendum is 'every two things... they are two contradictories'.
2
Extract the definiens
Find the condition that makes two things contradictories. It is 'one of them is the negation of the other'.
This is the core defining condition.
3
Check the scope
Notice that the author explicitly includes both concepts (taṣawwurāt) and assents (taṣdīqāt). Contradiction is not limited to propositions.
This extension is important for later applications.
4
Verify the definition's completeness
Does this definition cover all cases of contradiction? The author states that the negation of something is its contradictory, and vice versa, so it is a mutual relation.
The definition is complete and reciprocal.

فصل في التناقض
(كُلُّ أَمْرَيْن)، سواء كانا تصورين أو تصديقين، (أَحَدُهُمَا رَفْعُ الْآخَرِ فَهُمَا نَقِيضَانِ)؛ لأن نقيض الشيء رفعه، والصحيح رفع كل شيء نقيضه، (وَمِنْ ثَمَّ قَالُوا إِنَّ التَّنَاقُضَ مِنَ النَّسَبِ الْمُتَكَرِّرَةِ)، كل نسبتين لا يتعقل كل منهما إلا ويتعقل الأخرى، فكل منهما نسبة متكررة، سواء كانتا من نوع واحد، كالأخوة؛ فإنها لا تتعقل إلا إذا اعتبر قيامها بشخصين، ويتعقلان معا، أو أنواع مختلفة، كالأبوة والبنوة، والمراد ههنا هو القسم الأول.
Chapter on Contradiction. Every two things, whether they are concepts or assents, one of which is the negation of the other, they are two contradictories; because the contradictory of a thing is its negation, and the correct view is that the negation of every thing is its contradictory. And from that they said that contradiction is among the repeated relations: every two relations, neither one of them is conceived except that the other is also conceived, so each of them is a repeated relation, whether they are of one type, like brotherhood, for it is not conceived except when its occurrence to two persons is considered, and they are conceived together, or of different types, like fatherhood and sonship. What is intended here is the first type.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage defines contradiction (tanāquḍ) and explains its nature as a relative concept. The author begins by stating that any two things, whether they are concepts (taṣawwurāt) or assents (taṣdīqāt), such that one is the negation (rafʿ) of the other, are termed contradictories (naqīḍān). The key idea is that the contradictory of something is its negation, and conversely, the negation of something is its contradictory. This establishes a mutual relationship. The author then clarifies that contradiction is a 'repeated relation' (nisba mutakarrira), meaning that the two relations involved (e.g., the relation of being the contradictory of X and the relation of being the contradictory of Y) are such that conceiving one necessarily entails conceiving the other. He illustrates this with examples: brotherhood (ukhuwwa) is a single relation that requires two persons, and it is conceived simultaneously for both. This is a relation of the same type. Alternatively, relation can be of different types, like fatherhood and sonship (ubūwa wa bunuwwa), where each relation depends on the other but they are distinct. In the context of contradiction, the intended meaning is the first type—a single relation that applies to both terms. The passage thus sets the stage for understanding that contradiction is not merely a property of propositions but a relational notion that applies to both concepts and assents.

Contradiction as a Repeated Relation
Author explains contradiction as a repeated relation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why contradiction is classified as a 'repeated relation' (nisba mutakarrira) and distinguish between same-type and different-type repeated relations.

Core Idea
Contradiction is a relation that cannot be conceived without its counterpart — a repeated relation.

The author expands on the nature of contradiction by introducing the concept of 'repeated relation'. This explains why the two contradictories are always conceived together: each one is a relation that implies the other. Understanding this helps grasp the intrinsic connection between a proposition and its negation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the term 'repeated relation'
The author says contradiction is among the 'repeated relations'. This means the relation of contradictoriness involves two relations that are necessarily co-conceived.
It is a technical term for relations where conceiving one requires conceiving the other.
2
Examine the example of brotherhood
Brotherhood (ukhuwwa) is a single relation that applies to two persons simultaneously; you cannot conceive of a brother without conceiving the sibling relation.
This is an example of a repeated relation of the same type.
3
Compare with different-type relations
Fatherhood and sonship (ubūwa wa bunuwwa) are distinct relations that depend on each other; each is a repeated relation but of different types.
This contrasts with brotherhood where only one type is involved.
4
Apply to contradiction
The author clarifies that contradiction falls under the first type: it is a single repeated relation that applies to both terms.
The negation relation is the same for both sides.

Concepts and Their Contradictories: Two Ways
Author addresses the claim that concepts have no contradictories and explains two ways to understand conceptual contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between existential and logical contradiction in concepts, and apply the two ways of forming conceptual contradictories.

Core Idea
Concepts do have contradictories—but only in the logical, not existential, sense.

This passage addresses a common objection: that concepts (taṣawwurāt) cannot have contradictories. The author clarifies that this objection refers to existential incompatibility, which indeed does not apply to concepts. However, he then explains two valid logical ways to conceive of contradictory concepts, which are crucial for understanding propositional negation and the law of non-contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
Find the sentence where the author states that concepts have no contradictories. Note that this is in a different sense than the standard doctrine.
2
Define the two senses of 'contradictory'
Recognize existential contradiction (two things cannot coexist in reality) vs logical contradiction (they cannot both be true of the same subject). The author says existential contradiction does not apply to concepts, but logical contradiction does.
3
Examine the first way
Take a concept and add a negation (salb) to it, forming an affirmative modified proposition (mūjiba muʿaddala). The resulting concept is 'maximally different' and cannot be true of the same subject.
4
Examine the second way
Take a concept and add a simple negation, forming a negative proposition (sāliba). The two concepts are contradictory in the sense that they cannot be simultaneously true and false of one subject.
5
Summarise the key distinction
Concepts in themselves are not existentially contradictory, but when embedded in propositions (as subjects or predicates), they form logical contradictories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنَّ لِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ، سواء كان تصورا أو تصديقا (نَقِيضا وَاحِدًا)، هو رفعه إن كان وجوديا، ومرفوعه إن كان سلبيا. (وَمَا قِيلَ: إِنَّ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ لَا نَقَائِضَ لَهَا فَهُوَ بِمَعْنًى آخَرَ)، وهو الشيء المخالف لشيء، بحيث يستلزم تحقق كل منهما في نفس الأمر رفع الآخر، ورفع كل ثبوت الآخر، ومن البين أن لا تناقض بهذا المعنى بين التصورات؛ إذ لا تعاند في تحققهما في نفس الأمر.
واعلم أنه يمكن أخذ النقيض في التصورات بوجهين، أحدهما أن يؤخذ تصور ثم يضاف إليه سلب، ويكون بحيث إذا اعتبر صدقه على شيء وعقد قضية انعقد موجبة معدولة، فيحصل مفهوم في غاية الخلاف من المفهوم الأول، فهذا المفهومان نقيضان، أي مفهومان متباعدان غاية التباعد، ولا يمكن اجتماعهما في الصدق على موضوع واحد، لا أن اجتماعهما في نفس الأمر غير ممكن؛ إذ يمكن صدقهما على موضوعين في نفس الأمر، ويمكن ارتفاعهما عن موضوع واحد، بأن يكون معدوما.
وثانيهما أن يؤخذ مفهوم باعتبار صدقه على شيء، ويضاف إليه سلب بسيط، بحيث إذا عقد منه قضية انعقد سالبة ولو اعتبر صدقه على شيء وعقد قضية انعقد موجبة سالبة المحمول. وهذان المفهومان نقيضان بمعنى أنهما لا يجتمعان صدقا وكذبا على موضوع واحد، لا أنه لا يمكن اجتماعهما
And indeed everything, whether it is a concept or an assent, has one contradictory, which is its negation if it is positive, and its negated thing if it is negative. And what was said: 'Concepts have no contradictories' is in another sense, which is a thing that is opposite to a thing such that the existence of each in reality necessitates the negation of the other, and the negation of each necessitates the affirmation of the other. It is obvious that there is no contradiction in this sense between concepts, since there is no mutual incompatibility in their existence in reality. Know that it is possible to take the contradictory in concepts in two ways. One is that a concept is taken, then a negation is added to it, such that if its truth about something is considered and a proposition is formed, an affirmative modified proposition is formed, and a concept is obtained that is extremely different from the first concept. So these two concepts are contradictories, i.e., two concepts that are maximally distant, and they cannot both be true of one subject, not that their coexistence in reality is impossible; for it is possible for them to be true of two subjects in reality, and it is possible for both to be absent from one subject, if it is non-existent. The second way is that a concept is taken with consideration of its truth about something, and a simple negation is added to it, such that if a proposition is formed from it, a negative proposition is formed. And if its truth about something is considered and a proposition is formed, an affirmative proposition with a negated predicate is formed. These two concepts are contradictories in the sense that they cannot be simultaneously true and false of one subject, not that their coexistence is impossible.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage clarifies the claim that concepts (taṣawwurāt) have no contradictories, and then presents two valid ways in which conceptual contradiction can be understood. The author first reaffirms that everything—whether concept or assent—has exactly one contradictory, defined as its negation. However, the criticism that concepts lack contradictories refers to a different meaning: that in external existence (fi nafs al-amr), two positive concepts can coexist without one negating the other, e.g., 'whiteness' and 'blackness' can exist in different bodies simultaneously. So in that sense, there is no contradiction. But the author offers two ways to conceive of contradictory concepts in logic:

First way: Take a concept (e.g., 'human') and add a negation ('not-human'), forming an affirmative modified proposition ('A is not-human'). The resulting concept 'not-human' is maximally different from 'human', and they cannot both be true of the same subject. However, they can both be false of a non-existent subject (e.g., the void). So this is a logical (propositional) contradiction, not an existential one.

Second way: Take a concept (e.g., 'human') and add a simple negation, forming a negative proposition ('A is not human'). Then consider the affirmation of the negated predicate ('A is not-human'—which is an affirmative with a negated predicate). These two—'human' and 'not human'—are contradictory in the sense that they cannot be simultaneously true and false of the same subject. This is the standard logical contradiction of quality.

The passage thus reconciles the apparent objection by distinguishing existential contradiction (impossible coexistence in reality) from logical contradiction (impossible coexistence in truth on a single subject). Concepts as such do not entail existential contradiction, but when embedded in propositions, they do form contradictories. This nuance is crucial for understanding the scope of the law of non-contradiction in logic.

تصور
نقيض واحد
سلب
موجبة معدولة
سالبة المحمول

B) They cannot both be true of the same subject.
C) They are mutually exclusive in meaning.
D) They are opposite in quality.

Key Takeaway
The doctrine that every thing has one contradictory applies to concepts only in the logical sense, not existential.

The Paradox of a Complete Totality of Concepts
Author argues that a totality of all concepts leads to contradiction and provides two solution strategies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the logical contradiction that arises from positing a totality of all concepts.

Core Idea
A set of all concepts is both increasable and complete—a contradiction.

This passage presents a dialectical problem: if there is a whole containing every concept, it has a relation to its parts, leading to absurdities. Let's unpack how the author shows this is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the totality
The author considers a whole (kull) such that no concept or relation escapes it. This is the set of all concepts.
2
Find the contradiction
Concepts are inherently increasable—you can always add another concept. But the totality is defined as complete (nothing escapes). So it is both increasable and non-increasable, which is contradictory.
3
Trace the further absurdities
From this contradiction, the author says it is possible that it necessitates other impossibilities, like the contradictory being a part of itself or the relation being identical to the related.
4
Summarize the dialectic
The author then presents an alternative formulation: such a totality has no instance at all, so no need to posit a contradictory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كل نسبة بحيث لا يشذ عنه نسبة فهذا الكل له نسبة إلى الأجزاء، ومنها هذه النسبة ، فله نسبة إليها ،أيضا فالنسبة عين المنتسب مع حكمهم بتغاير النسبة للمنتسبين . ، (وَحَلُّهُ: أَنَّ اعْتِبَارَ الْمَفْهُومَاتِ لَا يَقِفُ عِنْدَ حَدٌ)؛ إذ المفهومات لا تقفية ؛ فإن كل جملة من المفهومات يمكن الزيادة عليها، وكذا النسب، (وَعَدَمُ الزِّيَادَةِ يَقْتَضِي الْوُقُوفَ إِلَى حَدَّ)، لا يمكن الزيادة عليه، (فَأَخْذُ الْجَمِيعِ كَذَلِكَ)، أي بحيث لا يشذ عنه شيء اعْتِبَارُ لِلْمُتَنَافِيَيْنِ)؛ لأن أخذ المفهومات ينادي على إمكان الزيادة، وعدم شذوذ شيء منه ينادي على امتناع الزيادة، فصار هذا المفهوم في قوة مجموع المفهومات التي يمكن الزيادة عليه ، ولا يمكن، وهو جمع بين المتنافيين فهو محال، فجاز أن يستلزم محالا آخر ، هو كون نقيض جزء للنقيض، أو كون النسبة عين المنتسب ، كذا «الحاشية» ، فَتَدَبَّرْ). (1) وربما يقرر هذا الجواب بأن كل المفهومات بحيث لا يشذ عنه شيء لا يصدق على شيء، وليس له مصداق أصلا، لا من الموجودات ولا من المعدومات؛ فإن كل موجود أو معدوم ليس بحيث يمكن الزيادة عليه ولا يمكن، فإن أريد برفع هذا المجموع رفع هذا المفهوم فليس جزء له، وإن أريد رفع مصداقه فليس له مصداق حتى يكون مفهوما ، فيطلب له نقيض ، فتأمل . ثم لا يخفى أن للسائل أن يعود ويقول: إن معلومات الباري تعالى الحاضرة عنده ليس مما يمكن الزيادة عليه أصلا، وإلا لزم الجهل بها، تعالى الله عن ذلك علوا كبيرا. فمجموع معلومات الله تعالى بحيث لا يشذ عنه معلوم مفهوم، فلا بد له من نقيض هو رفع هذا المجموع، وهو أيضا معلوم للباري ، فهو أيضا داخل في هذا المجموع ، فالجزء نقيض الكل. فالصواب في الحل أن يقال: إن مجموع المفهومات مفهوم تصوري ومركب خارجي، وكل مفهوم جزء خارجي لا يحمل على الكل أصلا، ولا هو مع الكل يحملان على ثالث ، فغاية ما لزم أن يكون نقيض مفهوم تصوري جزء خارجيا له، ولا نسلم استحالة ذلك، إنما يستحيل صدقهما على موضوع واحد، وهو غير لازم؛ فإن مجموع المفهومات ،رفعه يستحيل صدقهما على شيء واحد. نعم، يستحيل كون النقيض جزء عقليا للنقيض ؛ فإن ذلك يوجب اجتماعهما على شيء واحد هو الفرد؛ لاستحالة انفكاك الذاتي، وهو مستحيل. هذا، والعلم الحقيقي عند علام الغيوب، العليم الخبير .
Every whole such that no relation escapes it, this whole has a relation to the parts, and from them this relation, so it has a relation to it as well, so the relation is identical to the related despite their judgment that the relation is different from the related objects. And its solution: that the consideration of concepts does not stop at a limit; for concepts are not limited; for every set of concepts can be added to, and likewise relations. And non-addition necessitates stopping at a limit that cannot be added to. So taking the totality in such a way that nothing escapes it is a consideration of two contradictories; because taking concepts indicates the possibility of addition, and the fact that nothing escapes indicates the impossibility of addition. So this concept becomes equivalent to a totality of concepts that can be added to and cannot, and it is a combination of contradictories, so it is impossible. Then it is possible that it necessitates another impossibility, which is the contradictory being a part of the contradictory, or the relation being identical to the related. Thus in the marginal commentary (al-Hashiya). So reflect. (1) And perhaps this answer is formulated by saying: 'Every totality of concepts such that nothing escapes it does not apply to anything, and has no instance at all, neither among existents nor non-existents; for every existent or non-existent is not such that addition to it is possible and impossible. If by negating this totality one means negating this concept, then it is not a part of it; and if one means negating its instance, it has no instance such that it would be a concept, so a contradictory is sought for it.' Then reflect. Then it is not hidden that the questioner may return and say: The information of God the Exalted that is present with Him is not something to which addition can be made at all, otherwise ignorance of it would follow—God is exalted above that greatly. So the total of God's information is such that no known concept escapes it, so it must have a contradictory which is the negation of this totality, and it is also known to God, so it is also included in this totality. Thus the part is the contradictory of the whole. The correct position in the solution is to say: The totality of concepts is a conceptual concept and an external composite, and every concept is an external part that is not predicated of the whole at all, nor does it and the whole together predicate a third. So the utmost that follows is that the contradictory of a conceptual concept is an external part of it, and we do not admit the impossibility of that; impossibility only occurs when they are true of one subject, and that is not necessary; for the totality of concepts, its negation is impossible to be true of one thing. Yes, it is impossible for the contradictory to be a mental part of the contradictory; for that would necessitate their coming together on one thing, which is the individual, due to the impossibility of the separation of the essential, and that is impossible. This, and true knowledge is with the Knower of the Unseen, the All-Knowing, the All-Aware.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical discussion on the impossibility of a totality of all concepts. It begins by setting up a problem: if there is a whole such that no relation escapes it, then that whole has a relation to its parts, leading to a paradox where the relation is identical to the related. The author then presents a solution (حل) from an earlier commentator: consideration of concepts does not stop at a limit—concepts are always increasable. Therefore, taking a totality that is both increasable (because it is a set of concepts) and non-increasable (because nothing escapes) is a contradiction. This contradiction then leads to further impossibilities, such as the contradictory being a part of itself or the relation being identical to the related. The author then offers another formulation of the answer: such a totality has no instance at all, so there is no need to posit a contradictory. An objection is raised based on God's knowledge: God's knowledge is complete and cannot be added to, so it seems to be such a totality. The correct answer distinguishes between a conceptual concept (مفهوم تصوري) and an external composite (مركب خارجي). The totality of concepts is a conceptual concept, and its negation is an external part, which is not impossible. The only impossibility is when two contradictories apply to one subject, which does not happen here because the totality and its negation cannot be true of the same thing. The passage concludes by affirming that true knowledge is with God.

Resolving the Paradox: Conceptual Concept vs External Composite
Author argues that a totality of all concepts leads to contradiction and provides a solution by distinguishing conceptual concepts from external composites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the distinction between a conceptual concept (mafhūm taṣawwurī) and an external composite (murakkab khārijī) to resolve the paradox of a totality of all concepts.

Core Idea
The contradictory of a conceptual concept is an external part, not a mental one—no impossibility arises.

After presenting the paradox, the author provides a solution: the totality of concepts is a conceptual concept, and its contradictory is an external part. This avoids the absurdity of self-contradiction. Let's see how this distinction works and how it addresses the objection about God's perfect knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish conceptual vs external
A conceptual concept is a mental representation; an external composite is a combination of real things in the world. The totality of all concepts is a conceptual concept, not an external composite.
2
Understand the contradictory as external part
The contradictory (nāqīḍ) of this totality is the negation of the entirety, which is also a concept. The author says this is an external part, meaning it is not part of the same mental concept but a separate entity.
3
Apply the condition for impossibility
Two contradictories are impossible only if they apply to the same subject. Here, the totality and its negation cannot be true of any one thing, so there is no contradiction.
4
Address the objection about God's knowledge
The questioner says God's knowledge is a complete totality. The author replies that God's knowledge is known to God as a totality, but its contradictory is also known to God, so it is included—but that does not create a logical impossibility because the two concepts do not apply to the same object.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كل نسبة بحيث لا يشذ عنه نسبة فهذا الكل له نسبة إلى الأجزاء، ومنها هذه النسبة ، فله نسبة إليها ،أيضا فالنسبة عين المنتسب مع حكمهم بتغاير النسبة للمنتسبين . ، (وَحَلُّهُ: أَنَّ اعْتِبَارَ الْمَفْهُومَاتِ لَا يَقِفُ عِنْدَ حَدٌ)؛ إذ المفهومات لا تقفية ؛ فإن كل جملة من المفهومات يمكن الزيادة عليها، وكذا النسب، (وَعَدَمُ الزِّيَادَةِ يَقْتَضِي الْوُقُوفَ إِلَى حَدَّ)، لا يمكن الزيادة عليه، (فَأَخْذُ الْجَمِيعِ كَذَلِكَ)، أي بحيث لا يشذ عنه شيء اعْتِبَارُ لِلْمُتَنَافِيَيْنِ)؛ لأن أخذ المفهومات ينادي على إمكان الزيادة، وعدم شذوذ شيء منه ينادي على امتناع الزيادة، فصار هذا المفهوم في قوة مجموع المفهومات التي يمكن الزيادة عليه ، ولا يمكن، وهو جمع بين المتنافيين فهو محال، فجاز أن يستلزم محالا آخر ، هو كون نقيض جزء للنقيض، أو كون النسبة عين المنتسب ، كذا «الحاشية» ، فَتَدَبَّرْ). (1) وربما يقرر هذا الجواب بأن كل المفهومات بحيث لا يشذ عنه شيء لا يصدق على شيء، وليس له مصداق أصلا، لا من الموجودات ولا من المعدومات؛ فإن كل موجود أو معدوم ليس بحيث يمكن الزيادة عليه ولا يمكن، فإن أريد برفع هذا المجموع رفع هذا المفهوم فليس جزء له، وإن أريد رفع مصداقه فليس له مصداق حتى يكون مفهوما ، فيطلب له نقيض ، فتأمل . ثم لا يخفى أن للسائل أن يعود ويقول: إن معلومات الباري تعالى الحاضرة عنده ليس مما يمكن الزيادة عليه أصلا، وإلا لزم الجهل بها، تعالى الله عن ذلك علوا كبيرا. فمجموع معلومات الله تعالى بحيث لا يشذ عنه معلوم مفهوم، فلا بد له من نقيض هو رفع هذا المجموع، وهو أيضا معلوم للباري ، فهو أيضا داخل في هذا المجموع ، فالجزء نقيض الكل. فالصواب في الحل أن يقال: إن مجموع المفهومات مفهوم تصوري ومركب خارجي، وكل مفهوم جزء خارجي لا يحمل على الكل أصلا، ولا هو مع الكل يحملان على ثالث ، فغاية ما لزم أن يكون نقيض مفهوم تصوري جزء خارجيا له، ولا نسلم استحالة ذلك، إنما يستحيل صدقهما على موضوع واحد، وهو غير لازم؛ فإن مجموع المفهومات ،رفعه يستحيل صدقهما على شيء واحد. نعم، يستحيل كون النقيض جزء عقليا للنقيض ؛ فإن ذلك يوجب اجتماعهما على شيء واحد هو الفرد؛ لاستحالة انفكاك الذاتي، وهو مستحيل. هذا، والعلم الحقيقي عند علام الغيوب، العليم الخبير .
Every whole such that no relation escapes it, this whole has a relation to the parts, and from them this relation, so it has a relation to it as well, so the relation is identical to the related despite their judgment that the relation is different from the related objects. And its solution: that the consideration of concepts does not stop at a limit; for concepts are not limited; for every set of concepts can be added to, and likewise relations. And non-addition necessitates stopping at a limit that cannot be added to. So taking the totality in such a way that nothing escapes it is a consideration of two contradictories; because taking concepts indicates the possibility of addition, and the fact that nothing escapes indicates the impossibility of addition. So this concept becomes equivalent to a totality of concepts that can be added to and cannot, and it is a combination of contradictories, so it is impossible. Then it is possible that it necessitates another impossibility, which is the contradictory being a part of the contradictory, or the relation being identical to the related. Thus in the marginal commentary (al-Hashiya). So reflect. (1) And perhaps this answer is formulated by saying: 'Every totality of concepts such that nothing escapes it does not apply to anything, and has no instance at all, neither among existents nor non-existents; for every existent or non-existent is not such that addition to it is possible and impossible. If by negating this totality one means negating this concept, then it is not a part of it; and if one means negating its instance, it has no instance such that it would be a concept, so a contradictory is sought for it.' Then reflect. Then it is not hidden that the questioner may return and say: The information of God the Exalted that is present with Him is not something to which addition can be made at all, otherwise ignorance of it would follow—God is exalted above that greatly. So the total of God's information is such that no known concept escapes it, so it must have a contradictory which is the negation of this totality, and it is also known to God, so it is also included in this totality. Thus the part is the contradictory of the whole. The correct position in the solution is to say: The totality of concepts is a conceptual concept and an external composite, and every concept is an external part that is not predicated of the whole at all, nor does it and the whole together predicate a third. So the utmost that follows is that the contradictory of a conceptual concept is an external part of it, and we do not admit the impossibility of that; impossibility only occurs when they are true of one subject, and that is not necessary; for the totality of concepts, its negation is impossible to be true of one thing. Yes, it is impossible for the contradictory to be a mental part of the contradictory; for that would necessitate their coming together on one thing, which is the individual, due to the impossibility of the separation of the essential, and that is impossible. This, and true knowledge is with the Knower of the Unseen, the All-Knowing, the All-Aware.

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical discussion on the impossibility of a totality of all concepts. It begins by setting up a problem: if there is a whole such that no relation escapes it, then that whole has a relation to its parts, leading to a paradox where the relation is identical to the related. The author then presents a solution (حل) from an earlier commentator: consideration of concepts does not stop at a limit—concepts are always increasable. Therefore, taking a totality that is both increasable (because it is a set of concepts) and non-increasable (because nothing escapes) is a contradiction. This contradiction then leads to further impossibilities, such as the contradictory being a part of itself or the relation being identical to the related. The author then offers another formulation of the answer: such a totality has no instance at all, so there is no need to posit a contradictory. An objection is raised based on God's knowledge: God's knowledge is complete and cannot be added to, so it seems to be such a totality. The correct answer distinguishes between a conceptual concept (مفهوم تصوري) and an external composite (مركب خارجي). The totality of concepts is a conceptual concept, and its negation is an external part, which is not impossible. The only impossibility is when two contradictories apply to one subject, which does not happen here because the totality and its negation cannot be true of the same thing. The passage concludes by affirming that true knowledge is with God.

The Problem of Negation of Absolute Negation
Author raises a problem about absolute negation and provides an answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical problem with absolute negation's contradictory and evaluate the correct answer.

Core Idea
Absolute negation encompasses both contradictories, so its negation negates both.

This passage from the logic text raises a subtle puzzle: if 'absolute negation' is a broader concept, its contradictory seems to be a particular instance of it, leading to a problematic coincidence. We will analyze the problem, critique a proposed answer, and understand the correct resolution.

Guided Path
1
Define absolute negation
Identify that absolute negation (salb mutlaq) is the broader concept that includes both negation of existence and negation of negation.
This is crucial for understanding the scope.
2
Identify the problem
The concept of absolute negation has a contradictory, which is its negation. That negation is itself a kind of negation, so it becomes a species of absolute negation. This leads to the contradictory being a genus for itself, causing coincidence in truth on some individuals.
The problem is self-referential.
3
Examine the proposed answer
Some scholars answer that the contradictory of negation of negation is not negation but negation of negation of negation, which is not predicated of the original.
This avoids the direct regress but creates a new problem.
4
Understand the correct answer
The author shows that the proposed answer fails because the negated term is at least a co-extensive necessary of its contradictory. The correct answer is that absolute negation encompasses both contradictories, so negating it is equivalent to negating both, resolving the paradox.
This removes the problem of the part being subsumed under the whole.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ههنا إشكال آخر، هو أن مفهوم السلب المطلق الذي هو أعم من سلب الثبوت وسلب السلب ،مفهوم ، فنقيضه سلبه، وهو حصة له، والسلب المطلق المسلوب نوع له، فيلزم أن يكون نقيض ذاتيا لنقيض، ويلزم اجتماعهما في الصدق على فرد سلب السلب. أجاب عنه بعض الأجلة أن السلب ليس نقيضا لسلب السلب، بل نقيضه سلب سلب السلب، وهو ليس محمولا عليه أصلا، ولا يخفى ما فيه؛ فإن المرفوع وإن سلم عدم كونه نقيضا للرفع لكنه لا أقل من أن يكون لازما مساويا لنقيضه ؛ فإن سلب سلب السلب مستلزم للسلب ،قطعا، فيلزم أن يكون اللازم المساوي لنقيض سلب السلب نوعا وذاتيا له فيلزم الخلف. فالصواب في الجواب أن يقال: إن السلب الأعم من سلب الوجود وسلبه من الأمور الشاملة للنقيضين، فرفعه في قوة رفع النقيضين، فلا استبعاد في كونه مندرجا تحت
Then here is another problem: that the concept of absolute negation, which is more general than negation of existence and negation of negation, is a concept. So its contradictory is its negation, and it is a particular instance of it. And absolute negation when negated is a species of it. So it follows that the contradictory is a genus for the contradictory, and it follows that they coincide in truth on an individual of negation of negation. Some great scholars answered that negation is not a contradictory of negation of negation, rather its contradictory is negation of negation of negation, and it is not predicated of it at all. And what is in it is not hidden; for the negated, even if it is conceded not to be a contradictory of the negation, nevertheless it is at least a co-extensive necessary of its contradictory. For negation of negation of negation necessarily implies negation, so it follows that the co-extensive necessary of the contradictory of negation of negation is a species and a genus for it, leading to regress. So the correct answer is to say: Absolute negation, which is more general than negation of existence and its negation, is among the things that encompass both contradictories. So its negation is equivalent to negating both contradictories, so there is no improbability in it being subsumed under...
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage presents a new problem concerning absolute negation (salb mutlaq). The problem is that the concept 'absolute negation' (which includes both negation of existence and negation of negation) is itself a concept. Its contradictory is its negation, which is a particular instance of it (since it is a kind of negation). This makes the contradictory a genus for the original concept, which leads to a problematic coincidence. One proposed answer distinguishes the negation of absolute negation from absolute negation itself, but the author finds it insufficient because even if it is not a direct contradictory, it is a co-extensive necessary. The correct answer is that absolute negation covers both contradictories, so its negation is equivalent to negating both, which resolves the problem. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the conclusion would be that there is no improbability in the part being subsumed under the whole.

Negation of Absolute Temporal and General Modal Propositions
Author defines negation of four modal propositions and raises a problem

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct contradictory (naqīḍ) of absolute temporal and absolute general modal propositions and explain the problem of the temporal condition attachment.

Core Idea
Negating a temporal proposition requires attaching the time to the subject, not to the negation.

In this lesson, we explore how to properly negate modal propositions that involve time. The author gives the rule for the four types but then uncovers a subtle problem: if the time condition attaches to the negation itself, the negation may fail. Let's work through the logic step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two modal proposition types
Recognize absolute temporal (al-waqtiyya al-muṭlaqa: 'Every S is P at a specific time') and absolute general (al-muntashira al-muṭlaqa: 'Every S is P at all times'). Note that each carries a temporal condition.
These are affirmative modal propositions.
2
State the rule for their negation
According to the passage, the contradictory of an absolute temporal affirmative is a possible temporal proposition that negates temporal necessity: 'It is possible that some S is not P at that time'. For absolute general, the contradictory is a possible perpetual proposition: 'It is possible that some S is not P at some time'.
The negation always involves possibility (imkān) and negation of necessity.
3
Understand the condition for the rule to work
The author explains that the negation is correct only if the temporal condition (ẓarf) attaches to the subject of the negation (marfū‘), i.e., it qualifies the predicate's attribution to the subject. If the condition attaches to the negation itself (raf‘), the negation becomes a 'qualified negation' and both affirmative and negative could be false, violating contradiction.
4
Examine the counterexample
Consider the statement 'Nothing of the moon is eclipsed necessarily at the time of Zayd's standing'. If the time condition attaches to the negation, this statement would be true (since the moon is not eclipsed at that time), but the original affirmative 'Everything of the moon is eclipsed necessarily at that time' is also false. Both cannot be false if they are contradictories. Hence the problem.
This shows the rule requires careful formulation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في التناقض
الحكم حال ذلك الاتصاف، فسلب المقيد، فسلب المقيد باتصاف الأفراد بالعنوان وسلب المقيد به متلازمان، فاندفع الشك، وعلى الله التكلان.
(وَ) النقيض (لِلْوَقْتِيَّةِ الْمُطْلَقَةِ الْمُمْكِنَةُ الْوَقْتِيَّةُ الْمَحْكُومُ فِيهَا بسَلْب الضَّرُورَةِ الْوَقْتِيَّةِ)، أي بالإمكان في وقت معين، وَلِلْمُنْتَشِرَةِ الْمُطْلَقَةِ الْمُمْكِنَةُ الدَّائِمَةُ الْمَحْكُومُ فِيهَا بِسَلْبِ الضَّرُورَةِ الْمُنْتَشِرَةِ)، أي بالإمكان في جميع الأوقات، والبيان على طبق ما مر مر في الضرورية.
كَذَا قَالُوا، وَذَلِكَ إِنَّمَا يَتِمُّ إِذَا كَانَ الطَّرْفُ فِي سَوَالِبِ هَذِهِ الْمُوَجَّهَاتِ الأربع: الوقتية المطلقة والمنتشرة المطلقة والوقتية الممكنة والممكنة الدائمة ظَرْفًا لِلْمَرْفُوع؛ حتى يكون سلب المقيد، (لَا لِلرفع)؛ حتى يكون سلبا مقيدا، فيجوز ارتفاعهما بارتفاع القيد . وتَتَبُّعُ كلامهم يحكم بأن الظرف قيد للرفع، حتى إن قولنا لاشيء من القمر بمنخسف بالضرورة وقت نهوق زيد» كاذب، فالإشكال على حاله باق في هذه القضايا. هذا، والله أعلم.
Chapter on Contradiction. The ruling is the state of that attribution. So the negation of the qualified, and the negation of the qualified by the individuals being described by the title and the negation of the qualified by it are mutually entailing, so doubt is repelled, and trust is in God. And the contradictory for the absolute temporal is the possible temporal in which is judged with the negation of temporal necessity, i.e., with possibility in a specific time. And for the absolute general, the possible perpetual in which is judged with the negation of general necessity, i.e., with possibility in all times. The explanation is in accordance with what has passed in the necessary. Thus they said. And that is only complete if the term in the negatives of these four modalities—absolute temporal, absolute general, possible temporal, and possible perpetual—is a condition for the negated, so that it is a negation of the qualified, not for the negation itself, so that it is a qualified negation, and both may be removed by the removal of the condition. But examining their words shows that the condition is a condition for the negation itself, such that our statement 'Nothing of the moon is eclipsed necessarily at the time of Zayd's standing' is false. So the problem remains in these propositions. This, and God knows best.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage defines the negation (naqīḍ) for four types of modal propositions: absolute temporal, absolute general, possible temporal, and possible perpetual. The author first states that contradiction involves the state of attribution, and that negating the qualified (i.e., the proposition with a temporal condition attached to the subject) and negating the subject being described by that condition are equivalent. He then gives the negations: for an absolute temporal affirmative (e.g., 'Every S is P at time t'), the negation is a possible temporal proposition that negates temporal necessity, meaning it asserts possibility (not necessity) at that specific time. For an absolute general affirmative (e.g., 'Every S is P at all times'), the negation is a possible perpetual proposition that negates general necessity, meaning possibility at all times. However, the author notes a problem: this analysis only works if the temporal condition (ẓarf) attaches to the subject of the negation (marfū‘), not to the negation itself (raf‘). But examining the scholars' usage, they treat the condition as attaching to the negation, which leads to counterexamples. For instance, 'Nothing of the moon is eclipsed necessarily at the time of Zayd's standing' is false because the moon is not eclipsed at that time, but if the condition is part of the negation, the negation might be true when it should be false. Thus the difficulty persists.

Key Takeaway
The correct negation of a temporal modal proposition requires the time condition to be a condition for the subject, not for the negation, to avoid a logical pitfall.

The Contradictory of Universal Compound Propositions
Author explains how to find the contradictory of a universal compound proposition and answers an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the contradictory of a universal compound 'ārifiyya proposition as an exclusive alternative disjunction and explain when a conditional or affirmative proposition can serve as the contradictory.

Core Idea
The contradictory of a compound proposition may be a conditional, not just a categorical.

In this passage, the author demonstrates how to find the contradictory of a universal compound proposition, specifically the 'ārifiyya khāṣṣa. He constructs an exclusive alternative disjunction from the contradictories of its parts. He then addresses an objection that this violates earlier conditions of contradiction, clarifying that those conditions apply only to the explicit contradictory, while here a broader sense includes equivalent necessary propositions. This lesson will guide you through this logical operation and the key distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the universal compound proposition
Start with the 'ārifiyya khāṣṣa, e.g., 'Some writer is moving his fingers while he is a writer, but not always.' Recognize it as composed of two propositions: a universal negative absolute and a particular affirmative perpetual.
The compound is a conjunction of two categoricals.
2
Find the contradictories of each part
The contradictory of the universal negative absolute is a particular affirmative perpetual. The contradictory of the particular affirmative perpetual is a universal negative absolute. These are the two disjuncts.
3
Form the exclusive alternative disjunction
Combine the two contradictories with 'either...or' in an exclusive sense (māni'at al-khuluw), so exactly one is true. This disjunction is the contradictory of the original compound.
Exclusive alternative ensures opposite truth value.
4
Understand the objection and the response
An objector notes that this violates the conditions of contradiction (difference in quality, unity of judgment). The author responds that those conditions apply only to the explicit contradictory (ṣarīḥ). Here, the intended contradictory is broader, including the equivalent necessary (lāzim musāwī). Thus a conditional proposition can serve.
This distinction allows flexibility in logical analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مطلقة عامة سالبة كلية فنقيضها دائمة موجبة جزئية، فأخذناهما ورددنا بينهما على سبيل منع الخلو، وقلنا إما بعض الكاتب ليس بمتحرك الأصابع حين هو كاتب، وإما بعض الكاتب متحرك دائما، فحصل نقيض العرفية الخاصة، ولما كانت صادقة كذب هذه المنفصلة. ولما كان لقائل أن يقول: قد سبق اشتراط الاختلاف كيفا في التناقض، وههنا أخذتم نقيض الموجبة المركبة موجبة مانعة الخلو، وقد سبق أيضا اشتراط وحدة النسبة الحكمية، وقد أخذتم في نقيض الحملية شرطية مانعة الخلو أجاب بقوله: (وَإِذَا أُرِيدَ مِنَ النَّقِيضِ هَهُنَا أَعَمَّ مِنَ النَّقِيضِ الصَّرِيحِ وَاللَّازِمِ الْمُسَاوِي) له فَلَا يُسْتَبْعَدُ فِي كَوْنِهِ شَرْطِيَّةٌ أَوْ مُوجَبَةٌ) أن ما ذكرنا سابقا من الشرائط إنما كان في النقيض الصريح، والمراد ههنا أعم من الصريح واللازم المساوي، ولا استبعاد في كون موجبة شرطية لازما مساويا لنقيض الموجبة الحملية.
A universal negative absolute [proposition] has as its contradictory a particular affirmative perpetual [proposition]. So we took both and formulated a disjunction between them by way of exclusive alternative, and we said: Either some writer is not moving his fingers while he is a writer, or some writer is perpetually moving. So we obtained the contradictory of the particular 'ārifiyya. When it was true, this disjunction was false. And because an objector might say: The condition of difference in quality in contradiction has already been stipulated, and here you have taken the contradictory of the affirmative compound as an affirmative exclusive alternative, and also the condition of unity of the judgmental relation has been stipulated, and you have taken as the contradictory of a categorical a conditional exclusive alternative, he answered by saying: (When the contradictory is intended here to be more general than) the explicit contradictory and the equivalent necessary [proposition], then it is not far-fetched that it is a conditional or an affirmative. That what we mentioned previously regarding conditions was only regarding the explicit contradictory, and what is intended here is more general than the explicit and the equivalent necessary. And there is no far-fetchedness in an affirmative conditional being an equivalent necessary for the contradictory of the affirmative categorical.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage is a demonstration of how to find the contradictory of a universal compound proposition, specifically the 'ārifiyya khāṣṣa. The author takes the two constituent propositions (a universal negative absolute and a particular affirmative perpetual), combines them in an exclusive alternative disjunction, and shows that this disjunction is the contradictory. Then an objector points out that this violates the earlier conditions of contradiction (difference in quality and unity of judgmental relation). The author answers that the conditions apply only to the explicit contradictory (naqīḍ ṣarīḥ), whereas here we intend a broader sense that includes the equivalent necessary (lāzim musāwī). So a conditional proposition can serve as the contradictory if it is equivalent. This clarifies the flexibility in logical analysis.

Key Terms
نقيض (naqīḍ): Defined broadly here to include both the explicit contradictory and the equivalent necessary proposition. [Note: In earlier texts, naqīḍ is strictly defined as direct contradictory; here it is broadened.]
صريح (ṣarīḥ): Explicit contradictory that meets all standard conditions of contradiction.
لازم مساو (lāzim musāwī): A proposition that necessarily follows from another and is equivalent to it in truth value.
مانعة الخلو (māniʿat al-khuluw): An exclusive alternative disjunction where exactly one disjunct is true.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the contradictory of the universal compound proposition 'Some writer is moving his fingers while he is a writer, but not always'?
A) Some writer is not moving his fingers while he is a writer.
B) Either some writer is not moving his fingers while he is a writer, or some writer is always moving his fingers.
C) Every writer is either always moving his fingers or never moving his fingers.
D) No writer is moving his fingers.

Key Takeaway
The contradictory of a universal compound proposition can be an exclusive alternative disjunction of the contradictories of its parts, and this may take the form of a conditional, provided it is an equivalent necessary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: Consider the compound proposition: 'Every scholar is either reading or writing, but not both simultaneously.' Construct its contradictory as an exclusive alternative disjunction following the author's method.
?

Immediate Inference
intermediate
5 min
Contradictory of Particular Compound Propositions
Author explains why a disjunction fails and gives the correct method using a disjunctive predicate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the correct contradictory of a particular compound proposition using a disjunctive predicate.

Core Idea
The contradictory of a particular compound is a categorical with a disjunctive predicate, not a disjunction.

When dealing with compound propositions that are particular in quantity, the method used for universal compounds fails. The key insight is that the two independent particular components are more general than the compounded particular, making their contradictories misaligned. In this lesson, we will learn the correct approach: constructing a categorical proposition with a disjunctive predicate applied to each individual subject.

Guided Path
1
Identify the particular compound proposition
Locate the compound proposition in the form 'Some A is B but not always' (e.g., 'Some animal is actually human but not always'). Note that it combines two properties (being human and not always) under a particular subject.
2
Understand why the disjunction method fails
The contradictory of a universal compound is a disjunction of exclusive alternative. But for a particular, the two independent particular propositions (e.g., 'Some animal is always human' and 'Some animal is never human') are more general. Since the contradictory of a more general is more specific, the disjunction's contradictory does not match the compound's contradictory.
The principle: naqīḍ al-aʿamm akhaṣṣ (the contradictory of the more general is more specific).
3
Apply the method of disjunctive predicate
Form a categorical proposition where the predicate is disjunctive, alternating between affirmation and negation for every individual of the subject. For the example, it becomes: 'Every individual of animal is either eternally human or not eternally human.'
This is a categorical with mardūd al-maḥmūl (disjunctive predicate).
4
Verify truth
Check that the constructed contradictory is true when original is false. In the example, the original is false (some animals are not human, but some are, etc.), and the disjunctive predicate statement is true because for each animal, it is either always human or not.
The original and the disjunction are both false, but the correct contradictory is true.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا الحكم الذي ذكر في المركبة الكلية (بِخِلَافِ الْجُزْئِيَّةِ)؛ فإن نقيضها ليست منفصلة مانعة الخلو؛ فَإِنَّ مَوْضُوعَ الْإِيجَابِ وَالسَّلْبِ فِيهَا وَاحِدٌ ، فَالْجُزْئِيَّتَانِ) المستقلتان (أَعَمُّ) من المركبة الجزئية؛ إذ الموضوع فيهما قد يكون متعددا، (وَنَقِيضُ الْأَعَمِّ أَخَصُّ مِنْ نَقِيض الْأَخَصَّ)، فنقيض المركبة الجزئية أعم، ونقيض الجزئيتين المستقلتين أخص، فلا يكون نقيضا لهما ولا مساويا له ولهذا قد يكذب الجزئية المركبة وتلك المنفصلة معا ؛ فإن قولنا بعض الحيوان إنسان بالفعل لا دائما كاذب، وقولنا إما كل حيوان إنسان دائما، وإما لا شيء من الحيوان بالإنسان دائما أيضا كاذب. (۱) كذا في الأصل، والأولى «بإنسان». (فَالطَّرِيقُ) في أخذ النقيض هُنَاكَ أَنْ تُرَدَّدَ بَيْنَ نَقِيضَيْ الْجُزْتَيْنِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَى كُلِّ فَرْدٍ مِنَ الْمَوْضُوعِ ، فَهِيَ قَضِيَّةٌ حَمْلِيَّةٌ مَرْدُودَةُ الْمَحْمُولِ) بين السلب والإيجاب، فالنقيض في المثال المذكور كل واحد واحد من أفراد الحيوان إما إنسان دائما أو ليس بإنسان دائما» ، وهو صادق.
This ruling mentioned regarding the universal compound is contrary to the particular [compound]; for its contradictory is not a disjunction of exclusive alternative. Because the subject of affirmation and negation in it is one, so the two independent particular [propositions] are more general than the particular compound; since the subject in them may be multiple, and the contradictory of the more general is more specific than the contradictory of the more specific. Thus the contradictory of the particular compound is more general, and the contradictory of the two independent particulars is more specific, so it is not a contradictory to them nor equivalent. For this reason, both the particular compound and that disjunction may be false together. For our statement: 'Some animal is actually human but not always' is false, and our statement: 'Either every animal is eternally human, or no animal is eternally human' is also false. (1) This is in the original, and better is 'by being human'. Therefore the method in taking the contradictory there is to alternate between the contradictories of the two parts with respect to every individual of the subject. So it is a categorical proposition with a disjunctive predicate between negation and affirmation. So the contradictory in the aforementioned example is: 'Every individual of animal is either eternally human or not eternally human,' and it is true.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage explains why the contradictory of a particular compound proposition cannot be a disjunction of exclusive alternative, unlike the universal compound. The reason is that the subject of affirmation and negation is one, making the two independent particulars more general; consequently, the contradictory of the more general (the disjunction) is more specific and thus not equivalent. The correct method is to construct a categorical proposition with a disjunctive predicate, applying affirmation or negation to each individual. This yields a true contradictory.

Key Terms
مركبة جزئية
محمول مردود
جزئيتان مستقلتان
نقيض الأعم أخص

D) No animal is ever human.

Key Takeaway
The contradictory of a particular compound proposition is a categorical proposition with a disjunctive predicate, not a simple disjunction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
